<p>The <b>Atlanta Falcons</b> are a professional <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> team based in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>. The Falcons compete in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL) as a member of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/National_Football_Conference" title="National Football Conference">National Football Conference</a> (NFC) <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_South" title="NFC South">South</a> division. The Falcons were founded on June 30, 1965, and joined the NFL in 1966<sup id="cite_ref-AtlantaFalcons1_6-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-AtlantaFalcons1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> as an <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Expansion_team" title="Expansion team">expansion team</a>, after the NFL offered then-owner <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rankin_Smith" class="mw-redirect" title="Rankin Smith">Rankin Smith</a> a franchise to keep him from joining the rival <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> (AFL).
</p><p>In their 59 years of existence, the Falcons have compiled a record of 3985126 (<span class="nowrap">3985126</span> in the regular season and <span class="nowrap">1014</span> in the playoffs), winning division championships in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1980 Atlanta Falcons season">1980</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1998 Atlanta Falcons season">1998</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2004 Atlanta Falcons season">2004</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2010_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2010 Atlanta Falcons season">2010</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2012_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2012 Atlanta Falcons season">2012</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2016 Atlanta Falcons season">2016</a>. The Falcons have appeared in two <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowls</a>, the first during the 1998 season in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIII" title="Super Bowl XXXIII">Super Bowl XXXIII</a>, where they lost to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1998_Denver_Broncos_season" title="1998 Denver Broncos season">Denver Broncos</a> <span class="nowrap">3419,<sup id="cite_ref-atlantafalcons2_7-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-atlantafalcons2-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></span> and the second 18 years later, a <span class="nowrap">3428</span> overtime loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_New_England_Patriots_season" title="2016 New England Patriots season">New England Patriots</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_LI" title="Super Bowl LI">Super Bowl LI</a>. They are the oldest major professional sports team in America with no championships.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-8"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons' current home field is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Stadium" title="Mercedes-Benz Stadium">Mercedes-Benz Stadium</a>, which opened for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2017 Atlanta Falcons season">2017 season</a>; the team's headquarters and practice facilities are located at a 50-acre (20&nbsp;ha) site in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Flowery_Branch,_Georgia" title="Flowery Branch, Georgia">Flowery Branch</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-9"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> northeast of Atlanta in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hall_County,_Georgia" title="Hall County, Georgia">Hall County</a>.
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc">
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="History">History</h2></div>
<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r1320445320">.mw-parser-output .hatnote{font-style:italic}.mw-parser-output div.hatnote{padding-left:1.6em;margin-bottom:0.5em}.mw-parser-output .hatnote i{font-style:normal}.mw-parser-output .hatnote+link+.hatnote{margin-top:-0.5em}@media print{body.ns-0 .mw-parser-output .hatnote{display:none!important}}</style><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_Atlanta_Falcons" title="History of the Atlanta Falcons">History of the Atlanta Falcons</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Professional_football_comes_to_Atlanta_(1962)"><span id="Professional_football_comes_to_Atlanta_.281962.29"></span>Professional football comes to Atlanta (1962)</h3></div>
<p>Professional football first came to Atlanta in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_American_Football_League_season" title="1962 American Football League season">1962</a>, when the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">American Football League</a> (AFL) staged two preseason contests, with one featuring the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_Denver_Broncos_season" title="1962 Denver Broncos season">Denver Broncos</a> vs. the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_Houston_Oilers_season" title="1962 Houston Oilers season">Houston Oilers</a> and the second pitting the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_Dallas_Texans_season" title="1962 Dallas Texans season">Dallas Texans</a> against the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1962_Oakland_Raiders_season" title="1962 Oakland Raiders season">Oakland Raiders</a>. Two years later, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/American_Football_League" title="American Football League">AFL</a> held another exhibition, this time with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_New_York_Jets_season" title="1964 New York Jets season">New York Jets</a> taking on the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1964_San_Diego_Chargers_season" title="1964 San Diego Chargers season">San Diego Chargers</a>.
</p><p>In 1965, after the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta%E2%80%93Fulton_County_Stadium" title="AtlantaFulton County Stadium">AtlantaFulton County Stadium</a> (then known simply as Atlanta Stadium) was built, the city of Atlanta felt the time was right to start pursuing professional football.<sup id="cite_ref-sivmsur_10-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-sivmsur-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> One independent group which had been active in NFL exhibition promotions in Atlanta applied for franchises in both the AFL and NFL, acting entirely on its own with no guarantee of stadium rights. Another group reported it had deposited earnest money for a team in the AFL.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-11"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>With everyone running in different directions, some local businessmen (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cox_Communications" title="Cox Communications">Cox Broadcasting</a>) worked out a deal and were awarded an AFL franchise on <span class="nowrap">June 8, </span> contingent upon acquiring exclusive stadium rights from city <span class="nowrap">officials.<sup id="cite_ref-atlgeta_12-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-atlgeta-12"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nhodsbr_13-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-nhodsbr-13"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></span> NFL <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_the_NFL_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="History of the NFL Commissioner">Commissioner</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pete_Rozelle" title="Pete Rozelle">Pete Rozelle</a>, who had been moving slowly in Atlanta matters, was spurred by the AFL interest and headed on the next plane down to Atlanta to block the rival league's claim on the city of Atlanta.<sup id="cite_ref-AtlantaFalcons1_6-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-AtlantaFalcons1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sivmsur_10-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-sivmsur-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nhodsbr_13-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-nhodsbr-13"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> He forced the city to make a choice between the two leagues;<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> by June 30, the city picked Rankin Smith and the NFL.<sup id="cite_ref-sivmsur_10-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-sivmsur-10"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nwwfst_15-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-nwwfst-15"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The AFL's original expansion plans in June 1965 were for two new teams <span class="nowrap">in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_American_Football_League_season" title="1966 American Football League season">1966</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-msafltadd_16-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-msafltadd-16"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-sr_17-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-sr-17"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></span> in Atlanta and <span class="nowrap">Philadelphia.<sup id="cite_ref-pfldojap_18-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-pfldojap-18"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup></span> It later evolved into the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="1966 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins</a> in 1966 and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_Cincinnati_Bengals_season" title="1968 Cincinnati Bengals season">Cincinnati Bengals</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1968_American_Football_League_season" title="1968 American Football League season">1968</a>. The NFL had planned to add two teams in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1967_NFL_season" title="1967 NFL season">1967</a>; the competition with the AFL for Atlanta forced the first to be added a year early in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_NFL_season" title="1966 NFL season">1966</a>. The odd number of teams (15) resulted in one idle team (bye) each week, with each team playing 14 games over 15 weeks (similar to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1960_NFL_season" title="1960 NFL season">1960</a>: 12 games over 13 weeks). The second expansion team, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1967_New_Orleans_Saints_season" title="1967 New Orleans Saints season">New Orleans Saints</a>, joined the NFL as planned in 1967 as its sixteenth franchise.
</p><p>The Atlanta Falcons franchise began when it was approved to begin play in 1966 by a unanimous vote of the NFL club owners on June 21, 1965.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Rozelle granted ownership nine days later on June 30 to 40-year-old <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rankin_Smith_Sr." class="mw-redirect" title="Rankin Smith Sr.">Rankin Smith Sr.</a>, an executive vice president of Life Insurance Company of Georgia. He paid $8.5 million, the highest price in NFL history at the time for a franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-AtlantaFalcons1_6-2" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-AtlantaFalcons1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Rozelle and Smith made the deal in about five minutes and the Atlanta Falcons brought the largest and most popular sport to the city of Atlanta.
</p><p>The Atlanta expansion team became the 15th NFL franchise, and they were awarded the first overall pick in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_NFL_draft" title="1966 NFL draft">1966 NFL draft</a> as well as the final pick in each of the first five rounds.<sup id="cite_ref-HOF1966_20-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-HOF1966-20"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> They selected consensus <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1965_College_Football_All-America_Team" class="mw-redirect" title="1965 College Football All-America Team">All-American</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linebacker" title="Linebacker">linebacker</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tommy_Nobis" title="Tommy Nobis">Tommy Nobis</a> from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1965_Texas_Longhorns_football_season" class="mw-redirect" title="1965 Texas Longhorns football season">University of Texas</a>, making him the first-ever Falcon. The league also held the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_NFL_Expansion_Draft" class="mw-redirect" title="1966 NFL Expansion Draft">expansion draft</a> six weeks later in which Atlanta selected unprotected players from the 14 existing franchises. Although the Falcons selected many good players in those drafts, they still were not able to win right away.<sup id="cite_ref-AtlantaFalcons1_6-3" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-AtlantaFalcons1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Atlanta team received its nickname on August 29, 1965. Miss Julia Elliott, a school teacher from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Griffin,_Georgia" title="Griffin, Georgia">Griffin</a>, was singled out from many people who suggested "<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcon" title="Falcon">Falcons</a>" as the nickname for the new franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-l481_21-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-l481-21"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> She wrote: "the Falcon is proud and dignified, with great courage and fight. It never drops its prey. It is deadly and has a great sporting tradition."<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-22"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-23"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Smith_family_era_(19662001)"><span id="Smith_family_era_.281966.E2.80.932001.29"></span>Smith family era (19662001)</h3></div>
<p>The Falcons' inaugural season was in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1966 Atlanta Falcons season">1966</a>, and their first preseason game was on August 1, a loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_Philadelphia_Eagles_season" title="1966 Philadelphia Eagles season">Philadelphia Eagles</a>. Under head coach <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Norb_Hecker" title="Norb Hecker">Norb Hecker</a>, Atlanta lost their first nine regular-season games in 1966; their first victory came on the road against the struggling <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_New_York_Giants_season" title="1966 New York Giants season">New York Giants</a> on November 20 in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Yankee_Stadium_(1923)" title="Yankee Stadium (1923)">Yankee Stadium</a>. Two weeks later, Atlanta won at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_Minnesota_Vikings_season" title="1966 Minnesota Vikings season">Minnesota</a>, and beat <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_St._Louis_Cardinals_(NFL)_season" title="1966 St. Louis Cardinals (NFL) season">St. Louis</a> in Atlanta the next week for their first home win.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The team finished with a 1121 record the next year, with the only win coming in Week 7 in a 2120 win over the Minnesota Vikings in 1967.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After a 03 start to the 1968 season, Hecker was dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-w020_26-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-w020-26"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Norm Van Brocklin finished out the season as head coach with a 29 record.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Van Brocklin continued to coach the team the next season. The team improved to a 68 record in 1969.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>
The Falcons had their first <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Monday_Night_Football" title="Monday Night Football">Monday Night Football</a> game in Atlanta during the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1970 Atlanta Falcons season">1970 season</a>, a 207 loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1970_Miami_Dolphins_season" title="1970 Miami Dolphins season">Miami Dolphins</a>. The team went 482 in 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The only two winning seasons in their first 12 years were <span class="nowrap"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1971_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1971 Atlanta Falcons season">1971</a> (761)</span> and <span class="nowrap"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1973_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1973 Atlanta Falcons season">1973</a> (95).</span></p><figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:1987_Atlanta_Falcons_Pocket_Schedule.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/1987_Atlanta_Falcons_Pocket_Schedule.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="294" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/4d/1987_Atlanta_Falcons_Pocket_Schedule.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="271" data-file-height="319"></a><figcaption>The Falcons' defense taking on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_Denver_Broncos_season" title="1985 Denver Broncos season">Denver Broncos</a> quarterback <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_Elway" title="John Elway">John Elway</a> during a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1985_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1985 Atlanta Falcons season">1985</a> game.</figcaption></figure>
<p>In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1978 Atlanta Falcons season">1978 season</a>, the 97 Falcons qualified for the playoffs for the first time and won the Wild Card game against the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_Philadelphia_Eagles_season" title="1978 Philadelphia Eagles season">Eagles</a> 1413.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-31"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The following week, they lost to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978_Dallas_Cowboys_season" title="1978 Dallas Cowboys season">Dallas Cowboys</a> 2720 in the Divisional Playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-32"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 1979 team regressed to a 610 record.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1980_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1980 Atlanta Falcons season">1980 season</a>, after a nine-game winning streak, the Falcons posted a franchise then-best record of 124 and captured their first NFC West division title. The next week, their dream season ended at home with a loss to the Cowboys 3027 in the divisional playoffs. In the strike-shortened <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1982 Atlanta Falcons season">1982 season</a>, the 54 Falcons made the playoffs but lost to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1982_Minnesota_Vikings_season" title="1982 Minnesota Vikings season">Minnesota Vikings</a>, 3024.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Falcons coach <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leeman_Bennett" title="Leeman Bennett">Leeman Bennett</a> was fired after the loss.<sup id="cite_ref-u989_35-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-u989-35"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The team then had losing seasons for the next eight years. Dan Henning was hired prior to the 1983 season.<sup id="cite_ref-n719_36-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-n719-36"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1989_NFL_draft" title="1989 NFL draft">1989 NFL draft</a>, the Falcons selected cornerback <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deion_Sanders" title="Deion Sanders">Deion Sanders</a> in the first round, who helped them for the next four years, setting many records for the franchise.<sup id="cite_ref-b377_37-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-b377-37"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> "Neon Deion" (a.k.a. "Prime Time") had a flashy appeal and helped bring media attention to one of the league's most anonymous franchises. Sanders was also famous for playing on major league baseball teams (<a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a>) while simultaneously playing in the NFL.
</p>
<figure class="mw-default-size mw-halign-right" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Atlanta_Falcons_at_Los_Angeles_Rams_1991-12-08_-_01_(Atlanta_Falcons_crop).jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/Atlanta_Falcons_at_Los_Angeles_Rams_1991-12-08_-_01_(Atlanta_Falcons_crop).jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="173" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/85/Atlanta_Falcons_at_Los_Angeles_Rams_1991-12-08_-_01_%28Atlanta_Falcons_crop%29.jpg/500px-Atlanta_Falcons_at_Los_Angeles_Rams_1991-12-08_-_01_%28Atlanta_Falcons_crop%29.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="615" data-file-height="426"></a><figcaption>The Falcons playing against the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Los_Angeles_Rams" title="Los Angeles Rams">Los Angeles Rams</a> during a 1991 away game.</figcaption></figure>
<p>After defeating the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_New_Orleans_Saints_season" title="1991 New Orleans Saints season">New Orleans Saints</a> in the NFC Wild Card game, the Falcons' <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1991 Atlanta Falcons season">1991 season</a> ended in a divisional playoff loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_Washington_Redskins_season" title="1991 Washington Redskins season">Washington Redskins</a>. In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1991_NFL_draft" title="1991 NFL draft">1991 NFL draft</a>, the Falcons selected quarterback <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brett_Favre" title="Brett Favre">Brett Favre</a> as the 33rd overall pick. During his rookie season, he played in two games where he amassed a record of four passing attempts with no receptions and two interceptions. The following February, Favre was traded to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_Green_Bay_Packers_season" title="1992 Green Bay Packers season">Green Bay Packers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-n048_38-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-n048-38"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1992_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1992 Atlanta Falcons season">1992</a>, the Atlanta Falcons opened a new chapter in their history moving into the newly constructed Georgia Dome, where the team has defeated all 31 other NFL teams at least once during its time there.<sup id="cite_ref-f128_39-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-f128-39"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Dan_Reeves_years_(19972003)"><span id="Dan_Reeves_years_.281997.E2.80.932003.29"></span>Dan Reeves years (19972003)</h4></div>
<p>In 1998, under recently acquired head coach <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dan_Reeves" title="Dan Reeves">Dan Reeves</a>, quarterback <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chris_Chandler_(American_football)" title="Chris Chandler (American football)">Chris Chandler</a> and running back <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jamal_Anderson" title="Jamal Anderson">Jamal Anderson</a> the "Dirty Bird" Falcons had their greatest season to date.<sup id="cite_ref-g435_40-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-g435-40"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-q170_41-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-q170-41"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On November 8, they beat the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> 4110, ending a streak of 22 losses at cold-weather sites. The team finished with a franchise-best 142 regular-season record and the NFC West division championship.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On January 17, 1999, the Falcons upset the top-seeded Vikings at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hubert_H._Humphrey_Metrodome" title="Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome">Hubert H. Humphrey Metrodome</a> in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_Championship_Game" title="NFC Championship Game">NFC Championship Game</a> 3027, in an exciting overtime victory. However, in their first-ever Super Bowl appearance, they lost 3419 to the defending champion <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Denver_Broncos" title="Denver Broncos">Denver Broncos</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXIII" title="Super Bowl XXXIII">Super Bowl XXXIII</a>.
</p><p>In the second game of the Falcons 1999 season, running back Jamal Anderson, who had been a key player in the Falcons' 1998 success, suffered a season-ending knee injury. The Falcons finished the season with a very disappointing 511 regular-season record.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In 2000, the Falcons suffered through another horrendous season finishing 412 and once again missing the playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_NFL_draft" title="2001 NFL draft">2001 NFL draft</a>, the Falcons orchestrated a trade with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Diego_Chargers" title="San Diego Chargers">San Diego Chargers</a>, acquiring the first overall pick (which was used on quarterback <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Vick" title="Michael Vick">Michael Vick</a>) in exchange for wide receiver-return specialist <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tim_Dwight" title="Tim Dwight">Tim Dwight</a> and the fifth overall pick (used on running back <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/LaDainian_Tomlinson" title="LaDainian Tomlinson">LaDainian Tomlinson</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-d282_45-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-d282-45"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons finished the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2001_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2001 Atlanta Falcons season">2001 season</a> with a record of 79 and missed the playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jessie_Tuggle" title="Jessie Tuggle">Jessie Tuggle</a> retired following 14 seasons in Atlanta.<sup id="cite_ref-a120_47-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-a120-47"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Arthur_Blank_era_(2002present)"><span id="Arthur_Blank_era_.282002.E2.80.93present.29"></span>Arthur Blank era (2002present)</h3></div>
<p>On December 6, 2001, billionaire <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Home_Depot" title="Home Depot">Home Depot</a> co-founder <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_M._Blank" class="mw-redirect" title="Arthur M. Blank">Arthur M. Blank</a> reached a preliminary agreement with the Falcons' Taylor Smith to purchase the team for a reported $545 million.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In a special meeting prior to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVI" title="Super Bowl XXXVI">Super Bowl XXXVI</a> in New Orleans on February 2, 2002, NFL owners voted unanimously to approve the deal.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The 2002 season saw the Falcons return to the playoffs with a regular-season record of 961, tying the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Pittsburgh_Steelers" title="Pittsburgh Steelers">Pittsburgh Steelers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It was Vick's first year as the starter, and the team, with newly acquired running back Warrick Dunn, delivered the Green Bay Packers their first home playoff loss ever with a 277 result in the Wild Card Round.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> A 206 loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donovan_McNabb" title="Donovan McNabb">Donovan McNabb</a>-led Philadelphia Eagles the following week, however, ended the Falcons' season.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On March 19, 2003, the Falcons presented their new logo.<sup id="cite_ref-NewFalconsLogo2003_53-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-NewFalconsLogo2003-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-AtlantaFalcons1_6-4" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-AtlantaFalcons1-6"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> During the 2003 preseason Vick broke his leg and missed the first 12 games of the season. After losing 7 straight games, the decision was made to fire head coach Dan Reeves.<sup id="cite_ref-t276_54-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-t276-54"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wade_Phillips" title="Wade Phillips">Wade Phillips</a> acted as interim coach for the final three games.<sup id="cite_ref-n808_55-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-n808-55"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Although the Falcons won 3 of their last 4 games after the return of Vick, they ended up with a 511 record that year.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Jim_Mora_years_(20042006)"><span id="Jim_Mora_years_.282004.E2.80.932006.29"></span>Jim Mora years (20042006)</h4></div>
<p>In 2004, a new head coach, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_L._Mora" title="Jim L. Mora">Jim L. Mora</a>, was hired and Vick returned for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2004 Atlanta Falcons season">full season</a>. The Falcons went 115, winning their third division title and earning a first-round bye into the playoffs. In the divisional playoffs, the Falcons defeated the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_St._Louis_Rams_season" title="2004 St. Louis Rams season">St. Louis Rams</a>, 4717, in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Dome" title="Georgia Dome">Georgia Dome</a>, advancing to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_Championship_Game" title="NFC Championship Game">NFC Championship Game</a>, which they lost to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Philadelphia_Eagles_season" title="2004 Philadelphia Eagles season">Eagles</a>, 2710.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2005 Atlanta Falcons season">Falcons</a> again fell short of achieving back-to-back winning seasons in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_NFL_season" title="2005 NFL season">2005</a>, going 88.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_NFL_season" title="2006 NFL season">2006</a>, Michael Vick became the first quarterback in league history to rush for more than 1,000 yards in a season, with 1,039.<sup id="cite_ref-z575_61-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-z575-61"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After finishing the season 79, however, coach Jim Mora was dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Bobby_Petrino">Bobby Petrino</h4></div>
<p><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bobby_Petrino" title="Bobby Petrino">Bobby Petrino</a>, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Louisville" title="University of Louisville">University of Louisville</a>'s football coach, replaced Mora.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Before the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007_NFL_season" title="2007 NFL season">2007 season</a> began, Vick was suspended indefinitely by the NFL after pleading guilty to charges involving dog fighting in the state of Virginia.<sup id="cite_ref-x199_64-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-x199-64"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On December 10, 2007, Vick received a 23-month prison sentence and was officially cut from the Atlanta roster.<sup id="cite_ref-b006_65-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-b006-65"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>For the 2007 season, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2007_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2007 Atlanta Falcons season">Falcons</a> were forced to start <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Joey_Harrington" title="Joey Harrington">Joey Harrington</a> at quarterback.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On December 11, 13 games into his first NFL season as head coach, Bobby Petrino resigned without notice to coach at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arkansas_Razorbacks_football" title="Arkansas Razorbacks football">University of Arkansas</a>, leaving the beleaguered players only a note in the locker room.<sup id="cite_ref-u444_67-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-u444-67"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Secondary Coach <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Emmitt_Thomas" title="Emmitt Thomas">Emmitt Thomas</a> was named interim coach for the final three games of the season on December 12. The Falcons ended the year with a dismal 412 record.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>After the tumultuous and disappointing 2007 season, the Falcons made a number of moves, hiring a new general manager and head coach, drafting a new starting quarterback, and signing a starting running back.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Mike_Smith_years_(20082014)"><span id="Mike_Smith_years_.282008.E2.80.932014.29"></span>Mike Smith years (20082014)</h4></div>
<p>On January 13, 2008, the Falcons named former Patriots director of college football scouting <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Dimitroff" title="Thomas Dimitroff">Thomas Dimitroff</a> General Manager.<sup id="cite_ref-f140_69-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-f140-69"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On January 23, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jacksonville_Jaguars" title="Jacksonville Jaguars">Jacksonville Jaguars</a> defensive coach and former linebackers coach for the 2000 Super Bowl champion Baltimore Ravens <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Smith_(American_football_coach)" title="Mike Smith (American football coach)">Mike Smith</a> was named the Falcons' new head coach.<sup id="cite_ref-b093_70-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-b093-70"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Chargers back-up running back <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Turner_(American_football)" title="Michael Turner (American football)">Michael Turner</a> agreed to a 6-year, $30 million deal on March 2.<sup id="cite_ref-p494_71-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-p494-71"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On April 26, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matt_Ryan_(American_football)" title="Matt Ryan (American football)">Matt Ryan</a> (quarterback from <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>) was drafted third overall in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_NFL_draft" title="2008 NFL draft">2008 NFL draft</a> by the Falcons.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-72"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>72<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons finished the 2008 regular season with a record of 115, and the #5 seed in the playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-73"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>73<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On December 21, 2008, Atlanta beat the Minnesota Vikings 2417 to clinch a wild card spot, earning a trip to the playoffs for the first time since 2004. The Falcons would go on to lose in the wild-card round of the 2008 NFL playoffs to the eventual NFC champion <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2008_Arizona_Cardinals_season" title="2008 Arizona Cardinals season">Arizona Cardinals</a>, 3024.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-74"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>74<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Matt Ryan started all 16 games in his rookie season and was named the Associated Press Offensive Rookie of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-75"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>75<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> First-year head coach Mike Smith was named 2008 NFL Coach of the Year.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-76"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>76<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although they failed to make the playoffs in 2009 the team rallied to win their final three regular-season games to record back-to-back winning seasons for the first time in franchise history. The Falcons defeated the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a> 2010 in the final game of the season to improve their record to 97.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-77"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>77<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2010, with a regular-season record of 133, the Falcons secured a third straight winning season, their fourth overall divisional title, and the top overall seed in the NFC playoffs; however, the Falcons were overpowered by the eventual <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_XLV" title="Super Bowl XLV">Super Bowl XLV</a> champion <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a> in the NFC Divisional Playoffs 4821.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-78"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>78<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-j469_79-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-j469-79"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>79<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons scored 414 points  the fifth-most in franchise history.<sup id="cite_ref-atlantafalcons2_7-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-atlantafalcons2-7"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The team sent an NFL-high and franchise-best nine players to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_Pro_Bowl" title="2011 Pro Bowl">2011 Pro Bowl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-80"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>80<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons made a surprise trade up with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Cleveland_Browns" title="Cleveland Browns">Cleveland Browns</a> in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2011_NFL_draft" title="2011 NFL draft">2011 NFL draft</a> to select <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Alabama_Crimson_Tide_football" title="Alabama Crimson Tide football">Alabama</a> wide receiver <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Julio_Jones" title="Julio Jones">Julio Jones</a> sixth overall. In exchange, the Falcons gave up their first-, second- and fourth-round draft picks in 2011, and their first and fourth draft picks in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-g659_81-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-g659-81"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>81<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Jones, along with teammates <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tony_Gonzalez" title="Tony Gonzalez">Tony Gonzalez</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Roddy_White" title="Roddy White">Roddy White</a>, have since been dubbed Atlanta's "Big Three" (based on their total number of reception yards).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-82"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>82<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On August 30, 2011, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sports_Illustrated" title="Sports Illustrated">Sports Illustrated</a> senior writer <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peter_King_(sportswriter)" title="Peter King (sportswriter)">Peter King</a>, who correctly predicted the 2011 Super Bowl, made his predictions for the 2011 season and picked the Falcons to defeat the San Diego Chargers in the 2012 Super Bowl.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-83"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>83<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons finished the season at 106, securing the fifth seed after a Week 17 beatdown of Tampa Bay in which the Falcons pulled their starters after leading 420 just 23 minutes into the game.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-84"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>84<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons then went on to play the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_York_Giants" title="New York Giants">New York Giants</a> in a 2011 NFC Wild Card Game at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MetLife_Stadium" title="MetLife Stadium">MetLife Stadium</a> in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/East_Rutherford,_New_Jersey" title="East Rutherford, New Jersey">East Rutherford, New Jersey</a>. The first half was a defensive struggle, with the first points coming off of a safety by the Falcons, giving Atlanta a 20 lead. In the second quarter, though, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eli_Manning" title="Eli Manning">Eli Manning</a> connected with <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hakeem_Nicks" title="Hakeem Nicks">Hakeem Nicks</a> for a short touchdown pass to make it 72 Giants heading into the second half. Then the Giants took control, as Manning threw for two more touchdown passes to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mario_Manningham" title="Mario Manningham">Mario Manningham</a> and Nicks and the defense completed its shutout of the Falcons to give the New York Giants the win, 242, and the Falcons their third straight playoff loss with Matt Ryan and Mike Smith.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-85"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>85<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> After the season, defensive coordinator <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brian_VanGorder" title="Brian VanGorder">Brian VanGorder</a> accepted a coaching job at <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Auburn_University" title="Auburn University">Auburn University</a>, and the offensive coordinator <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mike_Mularkey" title="Mike Mularkey">Mike Mularkey</a> took the head coaching job in Jacksonville.<sup id="cite_ref-o068_86-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-o068-86"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>86<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Atlanta exploded out of the gate, going a franchise-best 80 and remaining the last unbeaten team in the NFL that year.<sup id="cite_ref-y604_87-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-y604-87"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>87<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Their hopes to get an undefeated season came to an end with a 2731 loss to the division rival Saints. Julio Jones had a remarkable second year, grabbing 10 touchdowns and 1,198 yards. The Falcons finished the season 133, and clinched the number one seed in the NFC playoffs.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-88"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>88<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-89"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>89<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons played the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Seattle_Seahawks" title="Seattle Seahawks">Seattle Seahawks</a> in their first playoff game. Although they went down 2827 with only 31 seconds left on the clock, Matt Ryan led the team to their first playoff victory, 3028.<sup id="cite_ref-f580_90-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-f580-90"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>90<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> It was the only playoff victory in the Mike Smith era.
</p><p>The Atlanta Falcons then advanced to face the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a>. The Falcons seized control of the game early with a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Matt_Bryant" title="Matt Bryant">Matt Bryant</a> field goal, a trio of Matt Ryan touchdown passes caught by Julio Jones and Tony Gonzalez coupled with outstanding defensive play. By the end of the half, the score was 2414. The tides of the game began to shift in the second half as the 49ers rallied back with a pair of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Gore" title="Frank Gore">Frank Gore</a> touchdown runs. Atlanta's offense attempted to reply but were ultimately shut down by the 49er defense. A few series later, late in the 4th quarter with little time remaining, Atlanta found themselves in a 4th and 4 situation at the 10-yard line. The Falcons needed just 10 more yards to secure victory and advance to their first Super Bowl berth in 14 years. Matt Ryan fired a pass to Roddy White which was ultimately broken up by inside linebacker <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NaVorro_Bowman" title="NaVorro Bowman">NaVorro Bowman</a>, resulting in a 2824 defeat.<sup id="cite_ref-a921_91-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-a921-91"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>91<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Following the success of the previous season, the Falcons were an expected Super Bowl contender. However, injuries hampered the team's performance and the team finished the season 412.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-92"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>92<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> With that, the streak of consecutive winning seasons came to an end and Mike Smith had his first losing season as a head coach. Tony Gonzalez, in his final season in the NFL, was selected to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_Pro_Bowl" title="2014 Pro Bowl">2014 Pro Bowl</a> as a starter representing Team Rice. Following the conclusion of the 2012 season, director of player personnel <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Les_Snead" title="Les Snead">Les Snead</a> departed the team to join the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/St._Louis_Rams" title="St. Louis Rams">St. Louis Rams</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Caldwell_(American_football_executive)" title="David Caldwell (American football executive)">Dave Caldwell</a>, assistant to general manager Thomas Dimitroff, left the team to join the Jacksonville Jaguars. <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Scott_Pioli" title="Scott Pioli">Scott Pioli</a>, former GM of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kansas_City_Chiefs" title="Kansas City Chiefs">Kansas City Chiefs</a>, was announced as the Falcons' new assistant GM. Mike Smith was given a one-year extension on his contract as head coach. The Falcons had the 6th overall pick in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2014_NFL_draft" title="2014 NFL draft">2014 NFL draft</a> with which they selected <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jake_Matthews_(American_football)" title="Jake Matthews (American football)">Jake Matthews</a>, who played as offensive tackle for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_A%26M" class="mw-redirect" title="Texas A&amp;M">Texas A&amp;M</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-b563_93-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-b563-93"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>93<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Despite having another rough season, the Falcons still had an opportunity to qualify for the playoffs at the end of the regular season. The Falcons hosted the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a> in their regular season finale, with the winners clinching the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_South" title="NFC South">NFC South</a> division. Unfortunately, the Falcons lost in a 343 blowout as Matt Ryan threw two interceptions that were returned for touchdowns and got sacked six times. The Falcons finished the season 610, marking the second consecutive losing season for the team.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-94"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>94<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The following day, Mike Smith was fired after seven seasons as head coach.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-95"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>95<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons would soon hire Seattle Seahawks defensive coordinator <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dan_Quinn_(American_football)" title="Dan Quinn (American football)">Dan Quinn</a> as the team's 16th head coach.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-96"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>96<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons had the 8th overall pick in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2015_NFL_draft" title="2015 NFL draft">2015 NFL draft</a> with which they selected <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Vic_Beasley" title="Vic Beasley">Vic Beasley</a>, a defensive end from Clemson University.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-97"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>97<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Dan_Quinn_years_(20152020)"><span id="Dan_Quinn_years_.282015.E2.80.932020.29"></span>Dan Quinn years (20152020)</h4></div>
<figure class="mw-default-size" typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Dan_Quinn_2015_intro_press_conference.jpg" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/Dan_Quinn_2015_intro_press_conference.jpg" decoding="async" width="250" height="146" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/Dan_Quinn_2015_intro_press_conference.jpg/500px-Dan_Quinn_2015_intro_press_conference.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="797" data-file-height="465"></a><figcaption><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dan_Quinn_(American_football)" title="Dan Quinn (American football)">Dan Quinn</a></figcaption></figure>
<p>In February 2015, the team was investigated by the NFL for alleged use of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Artificial_crowd_noise" title="Artificial crowd noise">artificial crowd noise</a> in the Georgia Dome.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-98"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>98<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons lost a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016_NFL_draft" title="2016 NFL draft">2016 NFL draft</a> selection as a result of the league's investigation.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-99"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>99<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Dan Quinn's first season saw a 50 start, the team's best start in four years. They would then struggle throughout the rest of the season by losing 8 of their last 11 games, resulting in an 88 record in the 2015 season.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-100"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>100<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> They did, however, give the Panthers their only regular-season loss. The Falcons used their first-round pick in the 2016 NFL draft on safety <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Keanu_Neal" title="Keanu Neal">Keanu Neal</a> from the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_Florida" title="University of Florida">University of Florida</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-101"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>101<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the Falcons' 25th and final season in the Georgia Dome, Atlanta lost their week 1 game to the Buccaneers 2431. The Falcons would then win their next four including one over the Panthers, when the franchise set new records: Matt Ryan threw for 503 yards, and Julio Jones caught 12 passes for 300 yards.<sup id="cite_ref-c681_102-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-c681-102"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>102<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Beating the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/San_Francisco_49ers" title="San Francisco 49ers">San Francisco 49ers</a> 4113 in Week 15, the Falcons improved to 95 and secured their first winning season since 2012. One week later, the Falcons defeated the Panthers in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte,_North_Carolina" title="Charlotte, North Carolina">Charlotte, North Carolina</a>, and clinched their first NFC South division title since 2012. In their last regular-season game at the Georgia Dome, the Falcons defeated the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">New Orleans Saints</a>, and secured an 115 record and a first-round bye.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-103"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>103<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the divisional round of the playoffs, Atlanta defeated the Seahawks 3620 in the Georgia Dome, and hosted their last game at the Georgia Dome against the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a> in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_Championship_Game" title="NFC Championship Game">NFC Championship Game</a> on January 22, 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-i265_104-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-i265-104"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>104<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons defeated the Packers 4421 to advance to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_LI" title="Super Bowl LI">Super Bowl LI</a> as the NFC champions.<sup id="cite_ref-p063_105-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-p063-105"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>105<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Atlanta was up 283 late in the third quarter, and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_England_Patriots" title="New England Patriots">New England Patriots</a> scored 31 unanswered points, with the last 6 in the first-ever overtime in the Super Bowl. The Patriots' 25-point comeback was the largest in Super Bowl history.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-106"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>106<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2016, the Falcons scored 540 points in the regular season, the seventh-most in NFL history, tied with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Greatest_Show_on_Turf" class="mw-redirect" title="Greatest Show on Turf">Greatest Show on Turf</a> (the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2000_St._Louis_Rams_season" title="2000 St. Louis Rams season">2000 St. Louis Rams</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-107"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>107<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, the Falcons defense gave up 406 points, 27th in the league.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-108"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>108<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons moved into their new home, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Stadium" title="Mercedes-Benz Stadium">Mercedes-Benz Stadium</a>, this season.<sup id="cite_ref-m391_109-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-m391-109"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>109<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Their first game ever played at the new stadium was a preseason loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arizona_Cardinals" title="Arizona Cardinals">Arizona Cardinals</a>. The first regular-season game at the new stadium was a rematch of the 201617 NFC Championship, with Atlanta defeating Green Bay 3423.<sup id="cite_ref-v944_110-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-v944-110"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>110<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Their first loss of the season was a 2317 home defeat to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buffalo_Bills" title="Buffalo Bills">Buffalo Bills</a> in week 4.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-111"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>111<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The team returned to the playoffs with a 106 record (albeit with a third-place finish in the NFC South). The Falcons defeated the Los Angeles Rams 2613 in the Wild Card round, but their 2017 season came to an end a week later in the Divisional Playoff round at the hands of the eventual Super Bowl champion Philadelphia Eagles 1510.<sup id="cite_ref-t115_112-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-t115-112"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>112<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-113"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>113<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The 2018 and 2019 seasons saw the Falcons go 79 and miss the postseason both years.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-114"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>114<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-115"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>115<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In their first game with new uniforms, the Falcons lost to the Seattle Seahawks at home 3825.<sup id="cite_ref-q087_116-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-q087-116"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>116<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons then suffered comebacks made by both the Cowboys on the road (3940) and then back in Atlanta against the Bears (2630).<sup id="cite_ref-i971_117-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-i971-117"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>117<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-u259_118-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-u259-118"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>118<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> On October 11, after the team suffered a 2316 loss at home against the Carolina Panthers and fell to 05, the Falcons announced the firings of Quinn and Dimitroff.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-119"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>119<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Defensive coordinator <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raheem_Morris" title="Raheem Morris">Raheem Morris</a> took over for the rest of the season, leading the team to a 412 record.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-120"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>120<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Morris was not retained after the season, and soon joined the Los Angeles Rams as their defensive coordinator.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-121"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>121<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Arthur_Smith_years_(20212024)"><span id="Arthur_Smith_years_.282021.E2.80.932024.29"></span>Arthur Smith years (20212024)</h4></div>
<p>On January 15, 2021, the Falcons announced that <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tennessee_Titans" title="Tennessee Titans">Tennessee Titans</a> offensive coordinator <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Arthur_Smith_(American_football,_born_1982)" title="Arthur Smith (American football, born 1982)">Arthur Smith</a> had been named the 18th head coach in franchise history.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-122"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>122<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Four days later, New Orleans Saints executive Terry Fontenot was named the Falcons' new general manager.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-123"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>123<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Tight end <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Kyle_Pitts" title="Kyle Pitts">Kyle Pitts</a> was selected with the 4th pick of the 2021 draft, and longtime star receiver Julio Jones was traded to the Titans, after publicly requesting a trade from Atlanta.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-124"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>124<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-125"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>125<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons improved on their record from the prior year, finishing the season with a 710 record.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-126"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>126<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>On March 21, 2022, the Falcons traded longtime star quarterback Matt Ryan to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Indianapolis_Colts" title="Indianapolis Colts">Indianapolis Colts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-127"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>127<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> During the 2022 season, the team finished last place in the NFC South with a 710 record.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-128"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>128<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The Falcons entered the 2023 seasons with heightened expectations after drafting <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Texas_Longhorns_football" title="Texas Longhorns football">Texas</a> running back <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bijan_Robinson" title="Bijan Robinson">Bijan Robinson</a> with the eighth overall pick of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2023_NFL_draft" title="2023 NFL draft">2023 draft</a> and making significant improvements in free agency, including signing <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jessie_Bates" title="Jessie Bates">Jessie Bates</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Calais_Campbell" title="Calais Campbell">Calais Campbell</a> to improve their defense.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-129"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>129<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> However, the team finished with a 710 record for the third consecutive season, although they had been in contention for a playoff spot until the final day of the season before a 4817 loss to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">New Orleans Saints</a> on January 7, 2024.<sup id="cite_ref-z604_130-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-z604-130"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>130<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The following day, Smith was fired after three years as head coach.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-131"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>131<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Raheem_Morris_years_(2024present)"><span id="Raheem_Morris_years_.282024.E2.80.93present.29"></span>Raheem Morris years (2024present)</h4></div>
<p>On January 25, 2024, the Falcons announced Raheem Morris's return to the organization, this time as the 19th head coach in Falcons history.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-132"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>132<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> During the early months of his tenure, Morris faced scrutiny and criticism for his questionable player selection decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-133"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>133<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Stadiums">Stadiums</h2></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Stadium" title="Mercedes-Benz Stadium">Mercedes-Benz Stadium</a></div>
<p>The Falcons have called three stadiums home in their 59 years of existence, and its third home in their history opened in the late summer of 2017. The first was the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta%E2%80%93Fulton_County_Stadium" title="AtlantaFulton County Stadium">AtlantaFulton County Stadium</a>, sharing with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Braves" title="Atlanta Braves">Atlanta Braves</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> team until 1991. In 1992, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Dome" title="Georgia Dome">Georgia Dome</a> was built, and the Falcons played there from its opening to the 2016 season. The Dome has been frequently used for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a>, including <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_State_Panthers_football" title="Georgia State Panthers football">Georgia State</a> football and college bowl games such as the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Peach_Bowl" title="Peach Bowl">Peach Bowl</a>.
</p><p>In an effort to replace the aging Georgia Dome and potentially host a future <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl" title="Super Bowl">Super Bowl</a>, team owner Arthur Blank proposed a deal with the city of Atlanta to build a new state-of-the-art stadium not far from where the Georgia Dome is located. Blank will contribute $800 million and the city of Atlanta will contribute an additional $200 million via bonds backed by the city's hotel/motel tax towards the construction of a retractable roof stadium. Blank will contribute additional money for cost overruns if it is needed. The team will provide up to $50 million towards infrastructure costs that weren't included in the construction budget and to retire the remaining debt on the Georgia Dome. In addition, Blank's foundation and the city will each provide $15 million for development in surrounding neighborhoods. Though the total cost of the stadium was initially estimated to be around $1 billion,<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-134"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>134<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> the total cost was revised to $1.5 billion according to Blank.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-135"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>135<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> In March 2013, the Atlanta City Council voted 114 in favor of building the stadium.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-136"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>136<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The retractable roof <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_Stadium" title="Mercedes-Benz Stadium">Mercedes-Benz Stadium</a> broke ground in May 2014, and became the third home stadium for the Falcons and the first for the new <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_United_FC" title="Atlanta United FC">Atlanta United FC</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Major_League_Soccer" title="Major League Soccer">Major League Soccer</a> club upon opening in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-137"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>137<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Logo_and_uniforms">Logo and uniforms</h2></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NFC-Throwback2-Uniform-ATL.PNG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/NFC-Throwback2-Uniform-ATL.PNG" decoding="async" width="150" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/11/NFC-Throwback2-Uniform-ATL.PNG/301px-NFC-Throwback2-Uniform-ATL.PNG 2x" data-file-width="301" data-file-height="331"></a><figcaption>Falcons uniform: 19711989</figcaption></figure>
