<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:NFC-Throwback-Uniform-ATL.PNG" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/NFC-Throwback-Uniform-ATL.PNG" decoding="async" width="150" height="165" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/3/35/NFC-Throwback-Uniform-ATL.PNG/301px-NFC-Throwback-Uniform-ATL.PNG 2x" data-file-width="301" data-file-height="331"></a><figcaption>Falcons uniform: 19972002</figcaption></figure>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Atlanta_falcons_unif_16.png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/Atlanta_falcons_unif_16.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="187" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Atlanta_falcons_unif_16.png/330px-Atlanta_falcons_unif_16.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/79/Atlanta_falcons_unif_16.png/500px-Atlanta_falcons_unif_16.png 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="637"></a><figcaption>Falcons uniform: 201619, including the throwback edition</figcaption></figure>
<p>The Atlanta Falcons' colors are black, red, silver and white.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-138"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>138<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> When the team began play in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1966 Atlanta Falcons season">1966</a>, the Falcons wore red helmets with a black falcon crest logo. In the center of the helmet was a center black stripe surrounded by two gold stripes and two white stripes. Those original colors represented the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Bulldogs" title="Georgia Bulldogs">Georgia Bulldogs</a>' red and black and the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Tech_Yellow_Jackets" title="Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets">Georgia Tech Yellow Jackets</a>' white and gold.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-139"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>139<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> Although the gold was removed after several seasons, the white remains to this day. They wore white pants and either black or white jerseys. At first, the falcon crest logo was also put on the jersey sleeves, but it was replaced by a red and white stripe pattern four years later. They switched from black to red jerseys in 1971, and the club began to wear silver pants in 1978. The facemasks on the helmets were initially gray, becoming white in 1978, and then black in 1984; the team wore black face masks until its 2020 redesign.
</p><p>A prototype white helmet was developed for the team prior to the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1974_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1974 Atlanta Falcons season">1974 season</a>, but was never worn.
</p><p>In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1990_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1990 Atlanta Falcons season">1990</a>, the uniform design changed to black helmets, silver pants, and either black or white jerseys.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-140"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>140<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The numbers on the white jerseys were black, but were changed to red in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1997_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="1997 Atlanta Falcons season">1997</a>. (The red numerals could be seen on the away jerseys briefly in 1990.)
</p><p>Both the logo and uniforms changed in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2003 Atlanta Falcons season">2003</a>. The logo was redesigned with red and silver accents to depict a more powerful, aggressive falcon, which now more closely resembles the capital letter <i>F</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-NewFalconsLogo2003_53-1" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-NewFalconsLogo2003-53"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-141"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>141<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Although the Falcons still wore black helmets, the new uniforms featured jerseys and pants with red trim down the sides. The uniform design consisted of either black or white jerseys, and either black or white pants. During that same year, a red alternate jersey with black trim was also introduced. The Falcons also started wearing black cleats with these uniforms.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-142"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>142<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_Atlanta_Falcons_season" title="2004 Atlanta Falcons season">2004</a>, the red jerseys became the primary jerseys, and the black ones became the alternate, both worn with white pants. In select road games, the Falcons wear black pants with white jerseys. The Falcons wore an all-black combination for home games against their archrivals, the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">New Orleans Saints</a>, winning the first two contests (2421 in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2004_NFL_season" title="2004 NFL season">2004</a> and 3617 in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2005_NFL_season" title="2005 NFL season">2005</a>), but losing 3113 in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2006_NFL_season" title="2006 NFL season">2006</a>. The Falcons wore the all-black combination against the New Orleans Saints for four straight seasons starting in 2004, With the last time being in 2007, losing 3414. They wore the combination again in 2006, against the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a> in Week 2. The Falcons won that game, 143. The Falcons also wore their all-black uniform in 2007 against the New York Giants, and in 2008 against the Carolina Panthers and against the Tampa Bay Buccaneers (for the second time). After that, the black pants and uniforms were retired and the white pants were now used full-time with the regular uniforms.
</p><p>In the 1980s, the Falcons wore their white uniforms at home most of the time because of the heat. When the Falcons started playing in a dome, the team switched to their dark uniforms for home games but have worn their white uniforms at home a few times since switching to the dome. It was announced at the 2009 state of the franchise meeting that the Falcons would wear 1966 throwback uniforms for a couple games during the 2009 season. The Atlanta Falcons wore 1966 throwback jerseys for two home games in 2009  against the Carolina Panthers on September 20 and against the Tampa Bay Buccaneers on November 29. The Falcons won both of those games. They donned the throwbacks again for 2 games in 2010, against Baltimore and San Francisco, winning both of those games as well. The throwbacks were used twice in 2011 and 2012; both times were against the Panthers and Saints. However, the throwbacks were retired following a 2013 NFL rule requiring only one helmet shell per team.
</p><p>The Falcons unveiled an all-red <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFL_Color_Rush" title="NFL Color Rush">Color Rush</a> uniform on September 13, 2016; however, due to the fact that the Falcons and the Tampa Bay Buccaneers had similar all-red Color Rush uniforms, the Falcons were unable to wear their Color Rush uniform until the 2017 season.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-143"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>143<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-144"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>144<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 2016, the Falcons unveiled a mixed throwback uniform set. The uniform tops, pants and socks closely resembled their 1960s kits. From 2016 to 2021, due to the NFL's one-shell rule, the Falcons wore the black helmets with the original logo decal similar to the design they wore in the 1990s. However, starting in 2022, with the NFL now reinstating the use of alternate helmets, the Falcons brought back the original red helmets to pair with their throwback uniforms.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-145"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>145<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>It was revealed in January 2020 that the Falcons will change uniforms for the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2020_NFL_season" title="2020 NFL season">2020 NFL season</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-146"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>146<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The ensuing design featured the return to black as the primary home uniform color for the first time since 2003. Both the primary home and road uniforms featured the "ATL" abbreviation in red above either white or black numbers with red drop shadows. The white and black tops are usually paired with either white or black pants. The alternate uniform featured a red/black gradient design and also featured the "ATL" abbreviation in white above white numbers with black drop shadows. Black pants are only used with this uniform. All three uniforms feature red side stripes. The current throwback uniform was also retained. In addition, the Falcons switched to matte helmets with the enlarged falcon logo and gray facemasks.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-147"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>147<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The red/black gradient alternates only lasted three seasons before it was removed from the uniform rotation in 2023.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-148"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>148<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Rivalries">Rivalries</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Divisional">Divisional</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="New_Orleans_Saints">New Orleans Saints</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcons%E2%80%93Saints_rivalry" title="FalconsSaints rivalry">FalconsSaints rivalry</a></div>
<p>The Falcons have shared a heated divisional rivalry with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/New_Orleans_Saints" title="New Orleans Saints">New Orleans Saints</a> (first the NFC West, and now the NFC South). The two teams were often basement-dwellers in the division; but the rivalry grew as a means of pride between the two cities, as they were the only two NFL teams in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Deep_South" title="Deep South">Deep South</a> for multiple decades. The series is the oldest and most iconic rivalry in the NFC South as the two teams have long harbored bad blood against one another.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-149"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>149<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The series is currently tied at 5555, including the most recent loss to the Saints on January 7, 2024, when the Falcons lost 4817.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-150"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>150<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Carolina_Panthers">Carolina Panthers</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Falcons%E2%80%93Panthers_rivalry" title="FalconsPanthers rivalry">FalconsPanthers rivalry</a></div>
<p>In addition, the Falcons share a similar, rivalry with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Carolina_Panthers" title="Carolina Panthers">Carolina Panthers</a>, with both teams having been in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_West" title="NFC West">NFC West</a> from the Panthers' founding in 1995 to the NFL realignment in 2002. Similar to their rivalry with the Saints, the Falcons have often endured several competitive divisional battles with the Panthers for lead of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_South" title="NFC South">NFC South</a>, though the two have yet to meet in the postseason. The series is also known as the "<b>I-85 Rivalry</b>"<sup id="cite_ref-Falcons_POV_151-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-Falcons_POV-151"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>151<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> due to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a> and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Charlotte,_NC" class="mw-redirect" title="Charlotte, NC">Charlotte</a> being only four hours apart on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Interstate_85" title="Interstate 85">Interstate 85</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-152"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>152<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-153"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>153<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons lead the series 3622.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-154"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>154<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</h4></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Buccaneers-Falcons_rivalry" class="mw-redirect" title="Buccaneers-Falcons rivalry">Buccaneers-Falcons rivalry</a></div>
<p>The Falcons share a less-intense divisional rivalry with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Tampa_Bay_Buccaneers" title="Tampa Bay Buccaneers">Tampa Bay Buccaneers</a> since the NFL realignment in 2002. The two had been regional opponents but very little had linked any further animosity towards the two as the Buccaneers played in the former <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/NFC_Central" class="mw-redirect" title="NFC Central">NFC Central</a> before the realignment.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-155"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>155<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-156"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>156<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-157"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>157<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The two teams would find themselves competing over staff and players alike, particularly during the 2000s after the Falcons had lured general manager <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Rich_McKay" title="Rich McKay">Rich McKay</a> after winning <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVII" title="Super Bowl XXXVII">Super Bowl XXXVII</a> the season prior.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-158"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>158<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> McKay's ties with Tampa extend into his family as his father <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/John_McKay_(American_football)" title="John McKay (American football)">John McKay</a> was head coach of the Buccaneers for nine seasons.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-159"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>159<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-160"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>160<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-161"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>161<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-162"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>162<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Conference">Conference</h3></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Philadelphia_Eagles">Philadelphia Eagles</h4></div>
<p>The Eagles lead the Falcons 21151, with a 31 lead in playoff games.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-163"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>163<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The rivalry first emerged after the Falcons upset the Eagles 1413 in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1978%E2%80%9379_NFL_playoffs#NFC:_Atlanta_Falcons_14,_Philadelphia_Eagles_13" title="197879 NFL playoffs">1978 Wild Card Round</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-164"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>164<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> and only intensified further in the 2000s thanks to the rivalry between prominent <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Dual-threat_quarterback" title="Dual-threat quarterback">dual-threat quarterbacks</a> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Donovan_McNabb" title="Donovan McNabb">Donovan McNabb</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Vick" title="Michael Vick">Michael Vick</a>. Recently, the Falcons lost to the Eagles in the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2017%E2%80%9318_NFL_playoffs#NFC:_Philadelphia_Eagles_15,_Atlanta_Falcons_10" title="201718 NFL playoffs">2017 divisional round</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-165"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>165<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-166"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>166<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-167"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>167<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Falcons managed a win against <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2024_Philadelphia_Eagles_season" title="2024 Philadelphia Eagles season">Philly</a> in week 2 en route to Philly's eventual <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Super_Bowl_LIX" title="Super Bowl LIX">Super Bowl LIX</a> victory.
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Green_Bay_Packers">Green Bay Packers</h4></div>
<p>The Falcons have also shared a playoff rivalry with the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Green_Bay_Packers" title="Green Bay Packers">Green Bay Packers</a> as much of the connections between the two teams stems from Atlanta trading future hall-of-fame quarterback <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Brett_Favre" title="Brett Favre">Brett Favre</a> to the Green Bay on February 11, 1992, in exchange for a first-round pick.<sup id="cite_ref-traded_168-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-traded-168"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>168<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-starts_169-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-starts-169"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>169<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The two teams have met four times in the postseason, most recently during the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2016%E2%80%9317_NFL_playoffs" title="201617 NFL playoffs">201617 NFC Championship</a> as it would also be the final game played at the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Georgia_Dome" title="Georgia Dome">Georgia Dome</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-170"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>170<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-171"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>171<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-172"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>172<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> The Packers lead the all-time series 1916, while both teams are tied in the postseason 22.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-173"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>173<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>

<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Atlanta_Falcons_starting_quarterbacks" title="List of Atlanta Falcons starting quarterbacks">List of Atlanta Falcons starting quarterbacks</a></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Draft_history">Draft history</h3></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Atlanta_Falcons_first-round_draft_picks" title="List of Atlanta Falcons first-round draft picks">List of Atlanta Falcons first-round draft picks</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons_draft_history" title="Atlanta Falcons draft history">Atlanta Falcons draft history</a>, and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/1966_NFL_expansion_draft" title="1966 NFL expansion draft">1966 NFL expansion draft</a></div>
<p>In the team's history, the Falcons have had the number one overall pick four times.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-206"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>206<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Coaching_staff">Coaching staff</h2></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="Head_coaches">Head coaches</h3></div>
<figure typeof="mw:File/Thumb"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:2024_Atlanta_Falcons_Raheem_Morris_OTA_Press_Conference_(cropped).png" class="mw-file-description"><img src="./Atlanta Falcons - Wikipedia_files/2024_Atlanta_Falcons_Raheem_Morris_OTA_Press_Conference_(cropped).png" decoding="async" width="250" height="312" class="mw-file-element" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/60/2024_Atlanta_Falcons_Raheem_Morris_OTA_Press_Conference_%28cropped%29.png/417px-2024_Atlanta_Falcons_Raheem_Morris_OTA_Press_Conference_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/60/2024_Atlanta_Falcons_Raheem_Morris_OTA_Press_Conference_%28cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="417" data-file-height="520"></a><figcaption><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Raheem_Morris" title="Raheem Morris">Raheem Morris</a> is the current Atlanta Falcons head coach.</figcaption></figure>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/List_of_Atlanta_Falcons_head_coaches" title="List of Atlanta Falcons head coaches">List of Atlanta Falcons head coaches</a></div>
<link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1320445320"><div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/History_of_Atlanta_Falcons_head_coaches" class="mw-redirect" title="History of Atlanta Falcons head coaches">History of Atlanta Falcons head coaches</a></div>
<p>In their history, the Atlanta Falcons have had 18 head coaches. Five coaches have served in interim roles<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-207"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>207<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-208"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>208<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</h2></div>
<p>The Falcons' flagship radio station is <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WZGC_(FM)" class="mw-redirect" title="WZGC (FM)">WZGC</a> 92.9 The Game.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-209"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>209<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup> <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Wes_Durham" title="Wes Durham">Wes Durham</a>, son of longtime <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/North_Carolina_Tar_Heels" title="North Carolina Tar Heels">North Carolina Tar Heels</a> voice <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Woody_Durham" title="Woody Durham">Woody Durham</a>, is the Falcons' play-by-play announcer, with former Atlanta Falcons quarterback and pro football veteran, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Archer_(quarterback)" title="David Archer (quarterback)">Dave Archer</a> serving as color commentator.<sup id="cite_ref-z104_210-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-z104-210"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>210<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-x946_211-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-x946-211"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>211<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_CW" title="The CW">The CW</a> affiliate <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WUPA" title="WUPA">WUPA</a> became the official television station of the Falcons, gaining rights to its preseason games, which are produced by <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/CBS_Sports" title="CBS Sports">CBS Sports</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-falcons-wupa_212-0" class="reference"><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atlanta_Falcons#cite_note-falcons-wupa-212"><span class="cite-bracket">[</span>212<span class="cite-bracket">]</span></a></sup>
</p><p>In the regular season, the team's games are seen on Fox's O&amp;O affiliate <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WAGA-TV" title="WAGA-TV">WAGA</a>. When the Falcons challenge an AFC team, CBS O&amp;O affiliate <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WUPA" title="WUPA">WUPA</a> will air those games while Sunday night games are televised on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/WXIA-TV" title="WXIA-TV">WXIA</a>, the local NBC affiliate.
</p>

<div class="mw-heading mw-heading4"><h4 id="Mississippi">Mississippi</h4></div>
<table class="wikitable">

<tbody><tr>
<th style="background-color: #000000 !important; color: #FFFFFF !important; box-shadow: inset 2px 2px 0 #A71930, inset -2px -2px 0 #A71930;;">City</th>
